# Window Size Study Report

## Scope
- Canonical inputs were rebuilt into four window sizes: 5s, 10s, 60s, and 300s.
- Canonical model suite: threshold baseline, isolation forest, autoencoder, GRU, LSTM, transformer, and tokenized LLM-style baseline.
- All experimental outputs were saved under `outputs/window_size_study/`.

## Why There Are So Many Variables
- The project monitors a full feeder, not a single device, so it tracks voltages, angles, power flows, DER states, controls, environment, and cyber events across many assets.
- Full-feeder monitoring creates hundreds of raw channels because each bus, line, phase, DER asset, and control element contributes separate measurements.
- Windowing multiplies those channels into multiple features because each signal is turned into statistics such as mean, standard deviation, min, max, and last value.
- Smaller windows can improve response latency because the detector can score more often, but they also expose more noise and short-lived fluctuations.
- Five-minute windows can be more stable because they smooth transient noise, but they can be slower for operational response.
